## Files created/modified across all phases

### CSS / JS (the design system)
- `styles/enhanced.css` — extended with: CSS variables, dark/light theme rules,
  sticky top nav, mobile hamburger, dark-mode polish for inline boxes, FAB-collapse
  auto-TOC styles, Phase 7 `.canvas-fallback` block (chat 12), and `!important`
  on the mobile `canvas { display: none }` rule (chat 15 — see *Phase 7 progress
  (chat 15)* below). Phase 1, 2, 3, 5, and 7 work all live here. Original
  `@media (prefers-color-scheme: dark)` block was rewritten to be conditional on
  `:root:not([data-theme="light"])` so the manual toggle wins.
- `styles/main.css` — **untouched** (legacy Eric Meyer reset + fixed-px margins).
  Hardcoded white on `.mermaid` containers and `!important` dark text on mermaid
  labels were addressed via overrides in `enhanced.css`, not by editing main.css.
- `js/course-enhancements.js` — **untouched** (mostly Prism.js bundle plus
  reading-time / progress-bar / keyboard-nav). Kept modular by design.
- `js/nav-enhancements.js` — **new file** containing: theme toggle (with localStorage
  persistence), mobile menu open/close, mermaid theme reinit on toggle, auto-TOC
  builder. All initialized on `DOMContentLoaded`.
- `js/clipboard.js` — **untouched**.

### Scripts (the migration tooling)

**All scripts and derived data live in `support/` as of chat 15** (folder gitignored — local-only, not deployed and not in version control).

- `support/inject_main_nav.py` — Phase 2. Already run. Injected nav block + script tag
  into all 64 lessons; upgraded mermaid `<script type="module">` to expose
  `window.__mermaid` and pick initial theme.
- `support/audit_lessons.py` — Phase 4. Bug-fixed for canvas size + section-ID counting.
  Re-run on Apr 29 2026 chat 11; outputs in `support/audit-post-phase6.csv` and
  `support/audit-post-phase6.md`. See *Audit findings* section below.
- `support/inject_section_ids.py` — Phase 5. **Never needed to run.** The post-Phase-6
  audit confirmed every h2/h3 in every lesson already has an `id` attribute.
  Script is kept for reference/safety net but should not be invoked.
- `support/wrap_canvas_fallbacks.py` — Phase 7. Idempotent, follows existing
  inject-script conventions. Auto-discovers `<canvas>` tags, injects fallback
  figure after each, skips already-wrapped canvases via lookahead, partitions
  catalog into ready/deferred by checking `images/components/<svg>` existence.
- `support/phase7-canvas-fallback-catalog.json` — Phase 7 catalog (chat 12). 15 lessons
  mapped, 3 reuse + 11 needs_new_svg as of chat 15 (was 12 needs_new_svg before
  chat 14 promoted `pygame_basics_game_loop.html` to reuse).

### Lessons (the content, after Phases 1–3)
- All 64 `*.html` lesson files have:
  - `<script src="...js/nav-enhancements.js" defer></script>` in `<head>`
  - `<nav class="main-nav">…</nav>` after `<body>` (preserving skip-to-main + progress-indicator placement)
  - Upgraded mermaid module init (where mermaid was present)
- `index.html` — **untouched by injection** (excluded by default). Has its own
  bespoke inline `<style>` block for course-hero + module-section. Doesn't
  currently flip on theme toggle. Decide whether to bring it into the system in
  a later phase.
- `genres_racing_python.html` — **misnamed**, actually a Python source file.
  Rename to `.py` (see Immediate Actions).

---

## Audit findings

### Post-Phase-6 audit (chat 11, Apr 29 2026) — `support/audit-post-phase6.csv` / `support/audit-post-phase6.md`

64 files analyzed (index.html excluded by default), average **453 words / 408 code lines per lesson** — basically unchanged from Phase 4 (471/402). Total: 63 mermaid diagrams, 53 canvas demos.

**Confirmed deltas vs Phase 4:**
- **Phase 6 SVG deployments visible in `img` column** (NOT `svg` — see Conventions below): 16 lessons gained Phase 6 SVGs, 21 total deployments (matches: 19 unique SVGs + pixel-grid in 2 lessons + sprite-sheet in 2 lessons). The audit `svg` column still reports 0 across the board because Phase 6 SVGs are external files embedded via `<img>`, not inline `<svg>` elements.
- **Section IDs are universal.** Every h2/h3 in every lesson already has an `id` attribute (perfect 1:1 match between heading count and id count, spot-checked across multiple lessons). Either authored that way from the start, or `inject_section_ids.py` was run silently in an earlier chat. Either way, the script doesn't need to run. Auto-TOC anchors are already in place.
- **No long outliers.** Max words/lesson 814 (publishing_updates), well under the 4000-word flag threshold.
- **48/64 lessons still have no static visuals** (mermaid only) — this number is now post-Phase-6 accurate (the 16 SVG-receiving lessons are correctly excluded because their img count > 0).
- **15 canvas-heavy lessons (>400k px²)** — these are the priority bucket for Phase 7 mobile fallbacks. Visible in the audit md: ai_behavior_trees, ai_state_machines, genres_puzzle, genres_racing, genres_rpg, genres_strategy, genres_tower_defense, networking_basics + 7 more (full list in CSV via canvas_px column).

**Universal gaps (every lesson):**
- 0 inline `<svg>` (Phase 6 ships externally; see above)
- 0 quizzes anywhere — Phase 8 target

**Outliers worth attention (post-Phase-6 audit):**
- `architecture_state_machines.html` — thinnest standalone lesson (315 words, 6 H2, 1 H3, 61 code lines, no exercise). Same outlier as Phase 4. Phase 8 candidate for restructuring.
- 3 `_python.html` companion files (`genres_puzzle_python.html`,
  `genres_strategy_python.html`, `genres_tower_defense_python.html`) — all
  lack both Summary and Exercise sections, look like code-only appendices.
  `genres_rpg_python.html` now has both (probably hand-added since Phase 4).
  Decide if the remaining 3 should be standalone or restructured.
- `networking_lobby.html` (1304 lines), `genres_tower_defense_python.html`
  (1100 lines), `networking_sockets.html` (864 lines), `sprite_groups_layers.html`
  (806 lines) — heavy code, candidates for `<details>`-collapsing the longest
  blocks behind a "show full code" toggle.

The audit's `has_summary` flag is permissive — it counts "What's Next" sections,
which are common. So a ✓ doesn't mean the lesson has a real "Key Takeaways" wrap-up.
A stricter pass is hand work.

---

## Phase 6 — SVG component library

Goal: hand-craft 10–15 reusable, theme-aware SVG templates that fill the gap
between abstract mermaid flowcharts and full canvas demos. They work on mobile
(canvas demos don't), they communicate spatial/structural concepts mermaid can't,
and they theme cleanly without depending on the lesson's CSS variables.

Live operational state — what's done, what's queued, locked decisions, visual
language, and recurring drawing conventions — all lives in **Phase 6 progress**
below. The original 15-item planning list and process sketch have been folded
into the live Queue and Decisions sections.

---

| 15 | `lighting-model.svg` | `graphics_lighting.html` (after Light Physics Analogy box, before Lighting Implementation in Python/ModernGL h2) | Phong lighting decomposition, viewBox 720×400, ID prefix `lm-`. Four spheres in a horizontal row at y=180 (radius 55, centers x=110/270/430/600) with "+" "+" "=" operators between (font-weight 300, size 32, slate axis color, y=190). **Sphere 1 — Ambient:** flat slate fill (`--lm-ambient-fill`), uniform constant base. **Sphere 2 — Diffuse:** radial gradient `lm-grad-diffuse` with fx/fy 28%/28% to place the apparent highlight upper-left; stops 0% bright blue → 38% mid blue → 100% dark base — Lambert's cosine falloff. **Sphere 3 — Specular:** dark base circle + overlay radial gradient `lm-grad-specular` with a tight white highlight (opacity stops 0%→6% solid → 14% at 0.4 alpha → 22%→0). **Sphere 4 — Final shading:** combined gradient `lm-grad-combined` layering all three — specular peak 0–6%, diffuse bright/mid 11–40%, ambient slate at 100% (no fully-black back, since ambient prevents it). Each sphere stacks 3 text lines: bold name (y=263), monospace formula (y=282) — `max(N · L, 0)`, `max(R · V, 0)^n`, `I = ambient + diffuse + specular` — and italic caption (y=300). **Light source:** sun glyph at (42, 58) — amber filled circle radius 12 with 8 cardinal/diagonal rays — labelled "light source". Single dashed amber directional ray from (62, 76) to (115, 129) with arrowhead via `lm-arrow-amber` marker, labelled "L". **Bottom notation strip:** rounded card x=40 y=334 w=640 h=50; line 1 keys out N/L/V/R/n with bold-tspan letters and middle-dot separators; line 2 italic note tying the three terms to the lesson's PBR shader ("diffuse becomes Lambertian + Fresnel; specular becomes Cook-Torrance"). Theme-aware via `prefers-color-scheme`: sphere palette uses theme-stable saturated mids and theme-flipping bright/base so the 3-stop gradients carry across modes. _(Shipped in a prior chat; logged here on Apr 29 2026 chat 8 sync pass.)_ |

| 17 | `parallax-layers.svg` | `platformer_parallax.html` (between Train Window Analogy and concept-tree mermaid) | Side-elevation depth diagram of the lesson's 5-layer Forest scene, viewBox 720×400, ID prefix `pl-`. **Five horizontal layer bands** stacked vertically (atmospheric perspective: top = farthest = faded, bottom = closest = saturated): all bands x=70, width=420, height=32, rx=4, gap 10. Footer caption at y=370: "Higher speedX → closer to camera. speedX > 1 means the layer scrolls faster than the camera itself." Two markers (`pl-arrow-amber`, `pl-arrow-blue`) follow the one-marker-per-color convention. Theme-aware via `prefers-color-scheme`. **Insertion location is non-conventional** — placed between the Train Window Analogy and the concept-tree mermaid (location A in the build proposal) rather than the established convention of between mermaid and Interactive Demo (location B used by scene-graph, pathfinding-grid, fov-cone, animation-strip, save-tree, component-diagram). Justified because the analogy IS implicitly a side-elevation: train = camera, world objects at varying depths from the train. The SVG visualizes the analogy literally, so pairing them directly is a stronger narrative than slotting into the conventional spot. |

### Decisions locked

- **Delivery:** standalone `.svg` files in `/images/components/`, embedded via `<img>` tag. Theming via internal `prefers-color-scheme` media query — **does NOT follow the lesson's manual `data-theme` toggle** (trade-off accepted for smaller HTML and reusability).
- **Cadence:** build one SVG, drop into one lesson, get review, iterate.
- **Insertion pattern:** `<figure class="svg-wrapper">` + `<img class="responsive-svg" loading="lazy">` + `<figcaption>`. The existing `.svg-wrapper` rule in `enhanced.css` already handles the light/dark figure background.
- **Paths:** absolute (`/images/components/...`) to match each lesson's existing path style.
- **CSS scoping inside the SVG:** `svg { --foo: ... }` rather than `:root { --foo: ... }`, so variables stay scoped if anyone ever inline-embeds.

### Visual language (use consistently across new SVGs)

- **Teal** light `rgb(13,148,136)` / dark `rgb(45,212,191)` — structure, control, surface, header
- **Blue (primary)** light `rgb(59,130,246)` / dark `rgb(86,156,214)` — content, users, main subject
- **Amber** light `rgb(217,119,6)` / dark `rgb(251,191,36)` — secondary force, validation, angles, friction
- **Red** light `rgb(220,38,38)` / dark `rgb(248,113,113)` — gravity / pulling-down (sparingly)
- **Slate grays** for axes, ticks, ground, neutral labels
- **Indigo (6th — promoted Apr 30 2026 chat 12)** light `rgb(124, 58, 237)` / dark `rgb(167, 139, 250)` — Tailwind violet-600 / violet-400. Reserved for the 6th categorical color when a chart genuinely needs 6+ distinct series (first use: easeOutBack in `easing-curves.svg`). Visually distinct from blue (cooler/saturated) and red (warmer). Use sparingly — most SVGs should still operate within the original 5-color palette.

### Recurring SVG conventions

- `role="img"` + `<title>` + `<desc>` inside the SVG; matching `alt` + `<figcaption>` outside.
- Subscripts via `<tspan dy="6" font-size="14">` (rendered reliably across browsers).
- One marker per colour (`head-gravity`, `head-normal`, …) — marker fills don't reliably inherit `currentColor` from the line referencing them.
- Draw connection lines before nodes so circles sit on top of their lines.

Decision rationale for both choices logged in *Open follow-ups on shipped SVGs* below.)_

- `pygame-primitives.svg` review items pending: (1) **`line` signature width-tightness** — cell 4's `line(surface, color, start, end, width)` is 39 chars at ~5.4 px/char monospace = ~211 px in a 224 px cell with text-anchor=middle, leaving ~6.5 px each side. Borderline. Programmatic getBBox overflow check (chat-20 addition) is the recommended source-level gate before render-check; if it overflows, two cheap fixes are (a) drop the optional `width` arg from the displayed signature (matching the bottom-strip note that width is already covered separately) which gives `line(surface, color, start, end)` at 32 chars, or (b) reduce the signature font from 10 to 9.5 px. (3) **Arc geometry** — sweep-flag=1 was chosen so the arc traces UP-OVER from start (637, 240) to stop (547, 240), which is the upper portion of the ellipse (matches pygame's CCW radians convention from start_angle=π/6 to stop_angle=5π/6). Verify on render that the arc visually "opens downward" i.e. the chord between endpoints is at the bottom of the arc, NOT at the top. If the arc renders flipped (sweep-flag should be 0), the visual immediately reads wrong against the labeled angles. - Decision (chat 20): chose **4 categorical colors (teal/amber/blue/red)** rather than the more economical 2-3 colors. The 4-color scheme maps semantic meaning per arg-type (position / size / line-end / arc-angle), which is the pedagogical money shot — a reader can scan a signature like `arc(surface, color, rect, start, stop)` and immediately see that 1 arg is teal-position, 2 args are red-angles. A 2-color scheme would have collapsed line-end (blue) into position (teal) and arc-angles (red) into size (amber), losing the per-arg-type color encoding.
- Decision (chat 20): used **inline triangle paths** for arrowhead glyphs in the dimension lines (cells 1, 2, 5) rather than `<marker>` elements. Markers don't reliably inherit `currentColor` (chat-19 lesson); inline paths use direct CSS class fills (`pp-dim-arrow`) which are theme-aware. Trade-off accepted: more verbose source for cleaner theme-flip behavior.
- Decision (chat 20): used **filled position dots with card-fill stroke halos** for the line cell endpoints (start = teal dot, end = blue dot). The halo provides visual contrast against the thick teal line stroke — without it, the teal start dot would visually merge with the line. Same technique used in screenshake-decay's amber jitter polyline endpoints.
- Decision (chat 20): chose to **show start dot in teal and end dot in blue** for the line cell, even though both are technically positions. The differentiation reinforces the signature reading: `line(surface, color, start, end, width)` has 3 distinct categorical args (start-position / end-position / size), and the visual mirrors the signature. Pure-teal-for-both would have lost that distinction.
- Decision (chat 20): used **sans-serif throughout the bottom strip** (3 lines of regular weight, no monospace). Continues chat-19's sans-serif-strip convention (originally introduced after chat-18's monospace-overflow incident). Wider per-character horizontal margin (~5.5–6 px sans vs ~6.3 px mono) and easier reading flow for prose-style explanations.
- Decision (chat 20): chose **3-line bottom strip** rather than 2 or 4. Line 1 is the universal rule (every primitive takes surface+color first); lines 2-3 are the two carve-outs (optional width arg, arc-specific radians convention). 2 lines would have crammed both carve-outs together; 4 lines would have spread the content too thin in the 68 px strip height.
- **Heads-up for future SVG drops:** before writing a new SVG, always check the target lesson(s) for an existing `<figure class="svg-wrapper">` block. `ai_state_machines.html` had one pointing at `/images/components/state-machine.svg` — that pre-staged markup dictated the layout, file naming, and content for SVG #6. `graphics_lighting.html` had TWO pre-staged blocks (`lighting-model.svg` and `sampling-kernel.svg`) with detailed alt-text specs that the SVG files match tightly.
- The mermaid concept tree directly after each newly-inserted SVG (in the lessons we touched) may feel redundant. Defer the keep-vs-replace decision until all SVGs are in.

### Phase 6 — render-check pass (Apr 30 2026 chat 16 — SVGs #17 / #18 / #19)

Render-check pass on the three Phase 6 SVGs flagged in *Open follow-ups on shipped SVGs* above. Browser session: Claude in Chrome against `http://localhost:5503`, window 1280×900, logical viewport ~1123×1834 (DPR 1.925), page `data-theme="light"`. **Important caveat — dark-mode visual not testable from this session.** Phase 6 SVGs theme via internal `@media (prefers-color-scheme: dark)` (locked Phase 6 decision); they do NOT respond to the page's manual `data-theme` toggle. Toggling `data-theme="dark"` on the parent page leaves the SVG in its light variant. Genuine dark-mode visual testing requires OS-level `prefers-color-scheme: dark`, which Claude in Chrome can't emulate from page-context JS. The dark-mode review items below are deferred to either (a) an OS-dark-mode eyeball pass on Ray's actual machine, or (b) reading each SVG's `<style>` block to confirm the dark-variant rules exist with the documented palette — carry forward to next chat.

**SVG #18 — `utility-response-curves.svg` in `ai_decision_making.html`:** verified clean in light mode at desktop width. (1) Vertical comparison line at `input=0.7` reads as a clear dashed slate reference axis — visually distinct from all 5 curves. (2) Intersection dots all visible: amber sigmoid (top, ~y=75), red gaussian (~y=146), slate linear (~y=122), blue quadratic (~y=177), teal exponential (bottom, ~y=215). White stroke (1.5 px) prevents merging with curve bodies; all 5 dots cleanly readable. (3) Legend formula readability good — `linear f(x) = x` / `quadratic f(x) = x²` / `exponential f(x) = x³ (power=3)` / `sigmoid k=10, c=0.5` / `gaussian c=0.5, w=0.2` all readable at rendered scale; sigmoid/gaussian shorthand notation reads as parameter labels, not as cryptic. (4) Worked-values 2-column 3-2 split (linear/quadratic/exponential at x=488; sigmoid/gaussian at x=588) is visually balanced — doesn't read as empty in the right column. (5) Z-order: sigmoid (drawn last) sits on top where it crosses other curves around x=0.5–0.6 — clean. Dark-mode tspan rendering pending file-source verification.

**SVG #19 — `easing-curves.svg` in `polish_tweening.html`:** verified clean in light mode at desktop width. (1) Asymmetric cell heights between rows (top 220×168 / chart 100 tall vs bottom 220×120 / chart 64 tall) read as deliberate — doesn't feel misaligned or unfinished. (2) Indigo `rgb(124, 58, 237)` for `easeOutBack` is visibly distinct from blue (cooler/saturated) and red (warmer) — the 6-color palette extension is working. (3) `easeOutElastic` peak (v≈1.27 at chart-y=35) clearly clears the v=1 reference line at chart-y=46 — peak does not get clipped at desktop width. (4) `easeOutBounce` multi-stage decay shows ~3 distinguishable bumps in the 64-px-tall bottom-row chart; the final small bump near t=1 is tight but visible — acceptable. (5) Chart-bg fill at the compressed 64-px bottom-row height has adequate visual weight — doesn't read as thin. **SVG #17 — `parallax-layers.svg` in `platformer_parallax.html`:** verified clean in light mode at desktop width. Image renders cleanly inside `<figure class="svg-wrapper">` (`naturalWidth: 270, naturalHeight: 150`), alt text intact. (a) Sky's 10-px arrow reads as a small amber wedge/triangle pointing left — marker-dominated as expected, but it does scan as a directional arrow, NOT a stray dot. The decay from Sky's wedge through Mountains' short line up to Foreground's long 120-px line gives a clean visual gradient of "barely moves → moves a lot." (b) Pill-row centering inside the callout reads as visually centered — the 5 pills (`SKY 10` / `MOUNTAINS 20` / `FAR TREES 40` / `NEAR TREES 70` / `FOREGROUND 120`) are evenly spaced and the row sits symmetrically within the callout box. The flagged 1-px asymmetry is below visual perception threshold at rendered scale. (c) Band stroke at `stroke-opacity=0.5` is visible against ALL 5 bands including the darkest (Foreground at 0.85 fill opacity) — stroke does not visually disappear. (d) Insertion location A (between Train Window Analogy and concept-tree mermaid) reads well: the analogy ends with "**The Train:** Your camera moving through the world" — SVG visualizes that camera-as-train metaphor concretely with a camera glyph + leftward apparent-motion arrows; the mermaid below then provides the structural taxonomy of the parallax system. The analogy → visualization → taxonomy → demo flow holds together. Convention-B swap (SVG below mermaid) is NOT needed. (e) Sign convention is technically correct but creates minor cognitive load: formula `offset = camera.x × layer.speedX` is positive, `Δx = +100 px` is positive, but per-band arrows point LEFT. The reader has to internalize that "offset" means "amount to subtract from layer's x-position so the layer appears to scroll left when the camera moves right." The figcaption + lesson prose mitigate this enough that it doesn't read as a bug — acceptable as-is.

**File-source dark-mode verification (completed this chat):** read all 3 SVG files via Filesystem MCP. All three have proper `@media (prefers-color-scheme: dark)` blocks with the documented dark-variant palette.

- `utility-response-curves.svg`: complete dark-mode CSS variables. They WILL theme-flip correctly in dark mode. Discharges the chat-15 "tspan dark-mode rendering" review item.
- `easing-curves.svg`: complete dark-mode CSS. All 6 curve colors including indigo `--ec-back: rgb(167,139,250)` flip properly. Bottom strip text and `Out`/`In`/`InOut` bold tspans use theme-aware `--ec-text` / `--ec-text-secondary` — will read correctly in both modes.

Camera glyph (`--pl-camera`), motion arrows (`--pl-arrow`), 5 graduated band fills (`--pl-band-far` through `--pl-band-near`, all teal-based), band strokes (`--pl-band-stroke`), and callout/pill backgrounds all flip. Notable detail: `--pl-camera-lens` flips from `rgb(255,255,255)` (light) to `rgb(15,23,42)` (dark) so the inner-lens contrast against the camera body is preserved in both modes — not an obvious oversight, intentional design.

**SVG #21 design highlights** (full description in *Done* table row above):
- Two stacked charts on a shared time axis. Top: trauma (linear). Bottom: shake offset on a *signed* Y axis, showing actual oscillating jitter inside a `±trauma²·max` envelope band. Showing *jitter inside envelope* rather than *just the envelope curve* is a richer pedagogical choice than the original todo's "two stacked decay charts" sketch — visually communicates that the player sees discrete oscillating offsets, not a smooth curve, and the envelope is the bound.

### Phase 6 progress (Apr 30 2026 chat 18 — SVG #21 render-check + bottom-strip overflow fix)

Closed the render-check loop on SVG #21 `screenshake-decay.svg` per the chat-17 todo. Render-check passed structurally; surfaced one real visual bug; fixed it; re-verified clean.

**Mobile-viewport workaround.** `Claude in Chrome:resize_window` reported success on a request to 380×820 but the host window stayed at outer 1233×2193 / inner 1123×1834. Probable cause: the MCP sidepanel takes ~110 px of the host width and the window manager refuses to shrink the host below the sidepanel's anchored minimum. Workaround that gave a clean true-mobile render: injected a same-origin `<iframe>` sized exactly 380×820 CSS px (`position: fixed; top:0; left:0; width:380px; height:820px;`) with `src` set to the lesson URL. Inside the iframe, `window.innerWidth` was a real 380 and `matchMedia('(max-width: 768px)').matches` was `true` — CSS `@media (max-width: 768px)` rules fire on the iframe's own viewport regardless of host window size. **For future Phase 7 render-checks in chat-MCP-sidepanel mode, the iframe-injection technique is the reliable substitute for actual window resize.** (Side note: the iframe doesn't reuse cached SVG fetches if you append a `?v=<timestamp>` cache-buster on the iframe `src` and on the SVG `src` after disk edits.)

**What rendered correctly on the first iframe pass.** `#shakeCanvas` computed `display: none` despite carrying inline `style="border: 1px solid #333; display: inline-block;"` — chat-15 `!important` hardening confirmed working in the field, not just in source. `figure.canvas-fallback` flipped to `display: block`, image loaded post-scroll (`naturalWidth: 270, naturalHeight: 150, complete: true`), figcaption rendered below. The Phase 6 figure (`figure.svg-wrapper`) at desktop position rendered too. Both states confirmed via combined desktop-host + mobile-iframe DOM probe.

**Real visual bug surfaced and fixed.** Review item #6 ("Bottom strip lesson-code line is dense") flagged a wrap concern, but the actual issue at render was overflow + clipping. The original single mono `<text>` at `x="60" y="390"` held a 127-character line `Lesson code: trauma -= decay_rate · dt   ·   shake = trauma * trauma   ·   offset_x = max_offset · shake · rand(−1, +1)` rendered with `.ssd-strip-mono` (10.5 px monospace). At ~6.3 px per character the line measured ~800 px wide. Bottom strip rect was `x="40" width="640"` so available text width was 620 px (text starts at x=60); SVG viewBox right edge was at x=720 so available before SVG-edge clip was 660 px. The line overflowed by ~180 px past both bounds and got visibly clipped at the SVG edge in BOTH desktop and mobile renders — final visible token in the screenshots was "...shake · rand" with the rest cut. Fix: split the single mono `<text>` into two `<text>` elements at `y="383"` and `y="395"`, and expand the strip rect from `y="363" height="32"` to `y="350" height="48"`; reposition prose from `y="378"` to `y="368"`. Wrap point chosen between the two assignments so each line is a complete statement: line 1 = `Lesson code: trauma -= decay_rate · dt   ·   shake = trauma * trauma` (~70 chars, fits comfortably); line 2 = `offset_x = max_offset · shake · rand(−1, +1)` (~46 chars). Inline HTML comment added at the rect documenting the chat-18 change. Re-verified at both phone (iframe with cache-buster) and desktop (host with cache-buster on `<img src>`) — all three lines render fully inside the strip with no clipping.

**SVG #21 review-item dispositions** (full original list in *Open follow-ups on shipped SVGs* above):

1. *Comparison line crosses inter-chart gap* — VERIFIED CLEAN. Dashed slate line at t=0.4 spans both charts continuously without visually clashing with the X-tick label row at y=186; ticks read cleanly in iframe render.
2. *Pseudo-random jitter polyline determinism* — VERIFIED CLEAN. The 26-point fixed-coordinate jitter reads as random oscillation, not a deliberate pattern.
3. *Right-card section redundancy* — STANDS AS-IS. The three sections (TRAUMA / OFFSET ENVELOPE / SIDE BY SIDE) at iframe width are visually clear and don't read as cluttered.
4. *SIDE BY SIDE bar widths* — VERIFIED CLEAN. The 64.8 px envelope bar reads as a bar at both viewports, including iframe width.
5. *Color choice teal trauma vs blue* — STANDS AS-IS. Teal/amber pairing reads correctly in light mode at both viewports.
6. *Bottom strip lesson-code line is dense* — RESOLVED THIS CHAT. See "Real visual bug surfaced and fixed" paragraph above.
7. *Mermaid coexistence* — STANDS AS-IS. Folded into broader keep-vs-replace decision.

All SVG #21 review items are now either verified, resolved, or stand-as-is per the dispositions above. SVG #21 ships clean as of chat 18.

**Process note.** The chat-15 lesson "source-level CSS reviews are insufficient — render-check at phone width is mandatory before declaring a Phase 7 wrap done" got a second instance this chat. Source review of SVG #21 in chat 17 had logged review item #6 only as a wrap concern at narrower viewports, not as an overflow concern in any rendering. The actual visible bug was clipping at the SVG edge — visible at ANY viewport, not narrow ones — and only surfaced once an actual rendered screenshot was inspected. Strengthens the discipline: source review catches structural correctness, render-check catches visual correctness, both are required.

**Text-overflow sanity check passes.** Bottom strip rect spans x=24–696 (width 672). Longest text line is row 3 sans-serif `→ — Sequence: runs children in order, fails on the first failure, succeeds if all succeed.` at ~89 chars. At 11.5 px sans-serif (~6 px/char), the line measures ~534 px wide; starting at x=44 it ends ~x=578. Comfortable margin against both the strip's x=696 right edge and the SVG viewBox's x=720 right edge. Importantly, the bottom strip uses **sans-serif throughout** (not monospace) — sans-serif at the same point size is ~5.5–6 px/char vs monospace ~6.3 px/char, giving substantially more horizontal margin during authoring. No `text-anchor: start` monospace landmines like SVG #21's chat-18 overflow case.

**SVG #22 design highlights** (full description in *Done* table row above):
- Single tree snapshot mid-tick rather than animated tick propagation. Static SVG can't show ticks fanning out over time, so the snapshot picks a moment that exhibits all four state colors at once: Combat=failure short-circuits the left branch, Survive=running with HP low?=success and Flee=running, Wander=idle (never tried). One frozen moment communicates Selector "try-until-non-failure" + Sequence "fail-on-first-failure" + Sequence success-cascade + 4-state color encoding all in one read.
- Amber active-path overlay (drawn AFTER default slate edges) traces only the running route — Root → Survive → Flee. Same draw-order technique as pathfinding-grid's gold path-line: highlight pops above the underlying graph mesh because of draw order, no z-index gymnastics.
- Composite-node badges use filled slate circles + bold white "?" / "→" symbols. The slate-circle background separates the symbol from the node text, keeping it readable at small render sizes where a symbol-on-text approach (just `?` next to "Selector") might blur the symbol into the label.

**Process note (chat 19 specific).** This is now the **second instance** of the "interrupted chat shipped artifacts that survived" pattern (chat 17 → SVG #21 was the first). Confirms the chat-17 working-conventions extension: artifact files written via Filesystem MCP are themselves a form of progress save, even when status.md hasn't been updated yet. The pre-build checklist's chat-17 addition — "check `images/components/<svg>.svg` doesn't already exist on disk before assuming the build is fresh" — caught this case correctly on chat-19 resume. Per Ray's chat-19 "lock in progress before pivoting" call (given the conversation-restart concern), the convention is now strengthened further: **save status.md updates as soon as substantial work is locked in, even before render-check, to make disk state self-documenting for the next chat**.

Render-check via iframe simulation deferred to a later chat segment as a clean rollback point.

### Phase 6 progress (Apr 30 2026 chat 20 — SVG #22 render-check closure + inline-SVG overflow check)

Closed the render-check loop on SVG #22 `behavior-tree.svg` per the chat-19 todo. Render-check passed all five verification points on the first iframe-simulation pass; no visible bugs surfaced. Both interrupted-chat carry-over instances (chat 17 → SVG #21 → chat-18 close, chat 19 → SVG #22 → chat-20 close) are now fully closed; the working pattern of "build in chat N, render-check in chat N+1" is established and carries forward to SVG #23.

**Iframe-simulation re-confirmed working** (chat-18 technique, second use). Same-origin `<iframe>` sized 380×820 injected into the host `ai_behavior_trees.html` tab; `src` set to `/ai_behavior_trees.html?v=rc<timestamp>` for cache-busting. Inside the iframe: `window.innerWidth: 380`, `devicePixelRatio: 2.475` (matches the chat-15 mobile-mode mapping — logical 380 → ~454 CSS px). All `@media (max-width: 768px)` rules fired correctly inside the iframe regardless of host-window dimensions. The iframe-injection technique is now the established replacement for `Claude in Chrome:resize_window` in MCP-sidepanel mode.

**Five verification points all clean:**

1. **`#behaviorCanvas` mobile hiding** ✓ — computed `display: none` despite carrying inline `style="border: 1px solid #333; background-color: #2C3E50; display: inline-block;"`. The chat-15 `canvas { display: none !important; }` hardening is now confirmed in the field for the third Phase 7 lesson (`ai_state_machines.html` chat 15, `polish_screenshake.html` chat 18, `ai_behavior_trees.html` chat 20).

2. **Phase 6 figure renders cleanly** ✓ — `<figure class="svg-wrapper">` between concept-tree mermaid and "Interactive Behavior Tree Demo" h2 sized 366×128 px, alt 304 chars intact. `<img>` at intrinsic 257×150 → rendered 346×202 (responsive scale-up; figure CSS clamps width, aspect ratio preserved).

3. **Main canvas-fallback figure renders** ✓ — `<figure class="canvas-fallback">` inside `.canvas-wrapper` at `display: block` on mobile, sized 346×177 with the same 257×150 → 346×202 img.

4. **Bottom-strip text fits inside viewBox** ✓ — parsed the SVG inline via `DOMParser` / `fetch` and measured all 20 `<text>` elements via `getBBox()` against the viewBox right edge. Max text-right at 666.4 px, viewBox right edge at 720, **53.6 px clearance margin, 0 overflows.** Sans-serif throughout in the bottom strip delivered the comfortable margin predicted in chat-19's source-level review (chat-18's `screenshake-decay` overflow case was monospace-driven, ~6.3 px/char vs sans-serif ~5.5–6 px/char).

5. **Tree-canvas fallback visibility-gating** ✓ — before clicking the "📊 Tree Visualization" toggle: `#treeView` `display: none` (inline + computed both `none`), tree-fallback figure `offsetWidth/Height: 0×0` (cascaded from parent). After click: `#treeView` flips to `display: block`, tree-fallback flips to `display: block` 326×367, and its `<img>` loads (257×150 → 326×190 rendered). Same chat-13 cosmetic pattern as `ai_state_machines.html` `#diagramCanvas` inside `<div id="stateDiagram">` — technically correct, just shallow indentation.

**Lazy-load timing reconfirmed (chat-15 finding).** First DOM probe after iframe load + 600 ms settle showed `imgComplete: false / naturalWidth: 0` on both visible imgs, even though `offsetWidth` was already populated (browser had reserved layout space). Forcing `loading="eager"` + `removeAttribute('loading')` + cache-buster src + `await img.decode()` resolved both to `complete: true / naturalWidth: 257`. Implication for future render-checks (now seen in three chats — chat 15, chat 18, chat 20): query `naturalWidth` AFTER scroll-into-view, OR force-eager + decode if probe timing is uncertain.

**Inline-SVG overflow check is a new programmatic tool.** Earlier chat-18 caught the `screenshake-decay` bottom-strip overflow only after the visual eyeball pass — this chat added a programmatic check: `fetch` the SVG file content, mount inline via `DOMParser`/`innerHTML` into an off-screen probe div, call `getBBox()` on every `<text>` element, compare each text's right edge against the viewBox right edge, flag any with overflow > 0.5 px. Returns counts + per-element measurements. **Cheaper than rendering and visually inspecting.** Could be used proactively on future SVGs as a final overflow gate before declaring source-level done. Not a substitute for visual eyeball (other classes of bug — color contrast, leader curves, badge legibility — are not captured), but it closes the specific monospace-text-overflow-at-strip-right-edge class of bug that surfaced in chat 18.

**Console errors during render-check (pre-existing, unrelated):** two error patterns in the iframe + host: (a) `TypeError: Prism.highlightElement is not a function` from `js/course-enhancements.js:313` — Prism syntax-highlighter loading order issue affecting all lessons, not introduced by SVG #22 work; (b) generic Chrome-extension async-listener message-channel-closed warning — noise from extension content scripts, not a page error. Neither relates to the SVG, the lesson markup, or the canvas-fallback rendering.

**SVG #22 review-item dispositions** (full original list of 8 items in *Open follow-ups on shipped SVGs* above):

1. *Snapshot-vs-animation tradeoff* — STANDS AS-IS. Static SVG renders cleanly at iframe width; figcaption clearly frames the snapshot as one tick of an animated process.
2. *Active-path amber overlay visibility* — VERIFIED CLEAN at iframe width. The two amber lines (Root→Survive, Survive→Flee) read as a distinct route above the slate edge mesh; not visually fighting the amber Selector / Survive / Flee node fills despite the upper-right amber clustering.
3. *"▶ running" indicator typography* — VERIFIED CLEAN at iframe width. Italic 10.5 px amber below Flee reads clearly; size + italic combination doesn't render as faint at the iframe's effective resolution.
4. *Composite-node badges* — VERIFIED CLEAN. Bold white "?" / "→" symbols on slate-circle backgrounds read at iframe scale; the "→" arrow's thin horizontal stroke does not anti-alias awkwardly.
5. *Wander leaf vertical positioning* — STANDS AS-IS. The 2-px offset between leaf rects (h=38) and composite rects (h=42) at level 1 doesn't read as a layout bug; consistent with size-per-node-type convention.
6. *Bottom-strip vertical density* — VERIFIED CLEAN by inline-SVG `getBBox()` overflow check. 4 rows + 2 dividers in 118 px height; no row's text intersects a divider line, all text fits within the viewBox right edge with 53.6 px clearance.
7. *Mermaid coexistence* — STANDS AS-IS. Folded into broader keep-vs-replace decision applying to all lessons.
8. *Second canvas-fallback nested inside togglable `#treeView`* — VERIFIED CLEAN. Toggle-click flips the parent visible, tree-fallback figure renders at 326×367 with img loaded; before toggle, fallback is correctly 0×0 due to parent display:none cascade.

All SVG #22 review items are now either verified, resolved, or stand-as-is per the dispositions above. SVG #22 ships clean as of chat 20.

### Phase 6 progress (Apr 30 / May 1 2026 chat 20 — SVG #23 build: pygame-primitives.svg)

Lock-in subsection for the SVG #23 build, written before render-check per the chat-19 "save status before pivoting" convention.

**Pre-build disk-state check ran clean** — `images/components/pygame-primitives.svg` did NOT exist on disk, lesson `pygame_basics_drawing.html` had no pre-staged figure markup or canvas-fallback wrappers. Genuine from-scratch build, unlike the chat-17 SVG #21 and chat-19 SVG #22 cases which both surfaced pre-staged artifacts from interrupted prior chats. Catalog entry's `build_concept` was followed faithfully (3×2 grid, 6 primitives, color-tinted signatures), refined into precise coordinates during the build.

**Why this lesson chose lowest-risk this chat.** Three candidates carried into chat 20 from chat-19's "next chat" notes: `pygame_basics_drawing.html` → `pygame-primitives.svg` (this build, 6 static primitives × signature labels), `polish_difficulty.html` → `difficulty-curves.svg` (3 sub-charts: linear / plateau / DDA), and `polish_sound.html` → `sound-layers.svg` (4 stacked audio waveforms). Picked the pygame-primitives target as Ray's "lowest risk" pick — well-scoped concrete concept (each cell is a single primitive with a fixed signature spec, no curve tuning or waveform fidelity judgment calls), strong existing convention for cell-grid layouts (mirrors easing-curves and component-diagram), and the catalog `build_concept` already specified the structure precisely.

**Visual language choices.**

- **Cell grid:** 3×2 with 8 px inter-cell gaps + 16 px outer margins. Each cell 224×152 with rounded corners + light card-fill stroke. Outer viewBox 720×420 matching established phase 6/7 convention.
- **ID prefix `pp-`** keeping with one-prefix-per-SVG pattern (`ssd-` for screenshake-decay, `bt-` for behavior-tree).
- **Color semantics — 4 categorical colors:** **teal** for positions (x, y, center, polygon points, line start, bounding rect — the largest category, used for the "anchor" arg of each primitive), **amber** for sizes (w, h, radius, line width — the "extent" arg), **blue** for the line's end endpoint (the only "secondary position" in the set, distinguished from start which is teal), **red** for arc angles (start_angle and stop_angle). Each color appears in both the visual demo's labels/dots AND the corresponding signature arg via colored `<tspan class>`.
- **Per-cell layout:** title at top (e.g. "rect"), demo shape in middle (~90 px tall area), monospace signature at bottom (`(surface, color, ...)` with arg names color-tinted). Demo uses small filled circles for position dots (teal/blue/red, with card-fill stroke halos for line endpoints to pop against the line stroke), short triangle paths for double-ended dimension arrows (no markers — the chat-19 lesson reinforced that markers don't reliably inherit currentColor), dashed slate for muted bounding shapes (`pp-bbox`), dashed teal for the arc's `rect` arg (`pp-bbox-pos`).
- **Bottom strip:** 3 sans-serif lines (continuing chat-19's wider-per-char-margin convention for strip text) — semantics that apply across ALL primitives (surface+color first), the optional width arg convention, and the arc-specific note about radians + CCW direction. One divider line between row 1 and row 2 visually separates "common to all" from "special cases".

**Tightest source-level constraint:** the `line(surface, color, start, end, width)` signature is 39 chars at ~5.4 px/char monospace = ~211 px wide, sitting in a 224 px cell with text-anchor=middle. Margins ~6.5 px each side. Borderline but should fit; **the programmatic getBBox overflow check (chat-20 addition for SVG #22) is the recommended source-level gate before render-check** — should walk all `<text>` elements (12 cell titles+signatures + 3 strip lines + ~14 inline labels) and verify each fits within its respective parent cell rect or strip rect. Particular focus on cell 4 (line) and cell 5 (ellipse — `ellipse(surface, color, (x, y, w, h))` at 38 chars also borderline).

**Lesson edits (single `Filesystem:edit_file` call, 3 edits):**

1. Inserted `<figure class="svg-wrapper">` (Phase 6 figure) immediately before `<h2 id="interactive-shape-drawing-demo">` — convention B placement, with contextual figcaption introducing the primitives reference and the inline color-coding legend ("position in teal, size in amber, the line's end point in blue, and arc angles in red").
2. Inserted `<figure class="canvas-fallback">` immediately after `<canvas id="shapesCanvas" width="600" height="400"></canvas>` — uses catalog `fallback_alt` and `fallback_caption` verbatim.
3. Inserted matching `<figure class="canvas-fallback">` after `<canvas id="spriteCanvas" width="600" height="400"></canvas>` — same fallback content per V1 limitation. The sprite canvas content (bouncing squares) is loosely related to the primitives diagram (still "drawing on a Pygame surface" theme); acceptable mismatch matching the chat-14 `pygame_basics_game_loop` decision.

**Catalog flipped:** `pygame_basics_drawing.html` status from `needs_new_svg` → `reuse (built chat 20)`.

## Phase 7 — Mobile fallbacks for canvases

### Phase 7 progress (Apr 30 2026 chat 12 — planning + scaffolding pass)

**Path 2 chosen: reuse + targeted SVG additions for the 15 canvas-heavy lessons.**

**Shipped this chat:**

- `phase7-canvas-fallback-catalog.json` — 15 lessons mapped. 3 reuse, 12 needs_new_svg (build concepts logged inline). Schema fields: `status`, `fallback_svg`, `fallback_alt` (short, for screen readers), `fallback_caption` (figcaption, contextual), `build_concept` (sketch for needs_new_svg only).
- `styles/enhanced.css` — Phase 7 — Mobile Canvas Fallbacks block added at end of file. New `.canvas-fallback` class hidden by default; `@media (max-width: 768px)` block makes it visible with responsive image + figcaption styling. Print rule hides it. Theming inherits from existing `.canvas-wrapper` (Phase 3 dark-mode polish covers it).
- `wrap_canvas_fallbacks.py` — idempotent, follows existing inject-script conventions. Auto-discovers `<canvas>` tags, injects fallback figure after each, skips already-wrapped canvases via lookahead, partitions catalog into ready/deferred by checking `images/components/<svg>` existence.

**Total: 12 canvases wrapped across 8 lessons through chat 22. 6 canvases (4 lessons) render-checked + CSS-hardened through chat 15; +1 canvas (polish_screenshake.html) wired chat 17 + render-checked clean chat 18 with bottom-strip overflow fix; +2 canvases (ai_behavior_trees.html) wired chat 19 + render-checked clean chat 20 with inline-SVG getBBox overflow check; +2 canvases (pygame_basics_drawing.html) wired chat 20 + render-checked clean chat 21 with cell-4 `line` signature width-tightness flag confirmed positive 3.45 px clearance via getBBox; +1 canvas (polish_difficulty.html) discovered already-shipped chat 21 + render-checked clean chat 22. 8 canvases deferred across 7 lessons pending 7 new SVGs (#25–#31).**

**V1 catalog limitation:** one `fallback_svg` per lesson (not per canvas). For lessons with 2 canvases, both canvases get the same fallback. That's pedagogically OK — mobile users miss both interactives, and a single themed diagram is enough context. If any lesson needs per-canvas fallbacks later, extend the catalog schema with a `canvases` map.

**Decisions locked:**

- **Markup pattern:** `<figure class="canvas-fallback">` with `<img class="responsive-svg">` + `<figcaption>` injected as a sibling of `<canvas>` inside the existing `.canvas-wrapper`. Indented 8 spaces to match typical lesson markup.
- **alt vs figcaption:** alt is a short, image-only description (one sentence); figcaption is the contextual caption tying the diagram back to the live canvas demo ("the interactive demo lets you …; this static diagram shows …").
- **Path style:** absolute `/images/components/...` to match the Phase 6 deployment pattern.
- **No SVG inlining for mobile.** Continued external-file delivery via `<img>` keeps Phase 6 conventions intact and lets the same SVG file serve both standalone Phase 6 figures AND Phase 7 fallbacks without duplication.
- **Don't suppress `.mobile-diagram-note`.** The 15 canvas-heavy lessons don't currently have one, but if any do, they coexist fine — the note is a paragraph, the fallback is a figure, both are display:block on mobile and stack naturally.
- **`build_concept` strings are sketches, not specs.** When picking up a needs_new_svg in a future chat, treat the build_concept as a starting suggestion. Read the lesson and refine before drawing — same workflow as Phase 6.

### Phase 7 progress (Apr 30 2026 chat 15 — render-check pass + CSS hardening)

Ran the phone-width render check on all 4 wrapped lessons (`ai_state_machines.html`, `networking_basics.html`, `polish_tweening.html`, `pygame_basics_game_loop.html`) via Claude in Chrome against `http://localhost:5503`. Window resized to 380×820 yielding `innerWidth: 454` (DPR 2.475 maps logical 380 to ~454 CSS px), `mobileMQ: true` confirmed via `window.matchMedia('(max-width: 768px)').matches`.

**CSS specificity bug discovered during render check.** 3 of the 6 canvases on the 4 wrapped lessons have inline `display: inline-block` on the `<canvas>` tag itself (set by the original lesson authors for layout). Inline styles win against element selectors on specificity, so the global mobile rule `@media (max-width: 768px) { canvas { display: none; } }` was being **overridden** — those canvases stayed visible at full width on mobile AND the `.canvas-fallback` figures rendered below them = duplicate content, not replacement.

**Affected canvases (pre-fix):**

| Lesson | Canvas | Inline `display:` | Pre-fix behavior |
|---|---|---|---|
| `ai_state_machines.html` | `#stateCanvas` | `inline-block` | bug — canvas + fallback both visible |
| `ai_state_machines.html` | `#diagramCanvas` | — | clean (rule applied) |
| `networking_basics.html` | `#networkCanvas` | `inline-block` | bug |
| `polish_tweening.html` | `#tweenCanvas` | `inline-block` | bug |
| `pygame_basics_game_loop.html` | `#gameLoopDemo` | — | clean |
| `pygame_basics_game_loop.html` | `#gameExamplesCanvas` | — | clean |

**Why undetected in chat 14:** chat 14's source-level review confirmed the canvas-fallback wrapping markup was clean per the script's contract, and read the head of `enhanced.css` to confirm the global `canvas { display: none; }` mobile rule existed. Both correct. The bug lived purely in CSS specificity, which a markup-level read can't catch. The chat 14 todo statement "the global `canvas { display: none; }` mobile rule applies regardless of wrapper" was factually true for the 3 unaffected canvases (right answer for the wrong reason — those happened to lack inline `display:`).

**Fix applied:** added `!important` to the `canvas { display: none; }` rule inside the `@media (max-width: 768px)` block in `styles/enhanced.css`. One-line CSS edit with 3 explanatory comments. Preemptive: now neutralizes inline `display:` on any current OR future canvas, so the deferred 11 lessons (SVGs #21–#31) don't need a per-canvas audit before wrapping.

```css
/* Hide canvas on mobile, show mobile message */
/* !important is required to beat per-canvas inline `display: inline-block`/`display: block` */
/* attributes that some lessons set for layout. Without it, those canvases stay visible */
/* on mobile and the .canvas-fallback figures render as duplicate content. */
canvas {
    display: none !important;
}
```

**Render check results post-fix:** all 4 wrapped lessons confirmed clean at phone width.

- `ai_state_machines.html` canvas #1: hidden ✓, fallback (`state-machine-ai.svg`, naturalW 281) renders ✓.
- `ai_state_machines.html` canvas #2: hidden ✓, fallback renders ✓ inside the toggled `#stateDiagram` panel after clicking the "State Diagram" button.
- `networking_basics.html`: canvas hidden ✓, fallback (`network-topology.svg`, naturalW 292) renders ✓.
- `polish_tweening.html`: canvas hidden ✓, fallback (`easing-curves.svg`, naturalW 270) renders ✓ — full 6-curve grid visible (linear / easeOutQuad / easeInOutCubic / easeOutBounce / easeOutElastic / easeOutBack) with the "Out = front-loaded · In = builds anticipation · InOut = both" footer band intact.
- `pygame_basics_game_loop.html` canvas #1 (`#gameLoopDemo`): hidden ✓, fallback (`game-loop-cycle.svg`, naturalW 257) renders ✓.
- `pygame_basics_game_loop.html` canvas #2 (`#gameExamplesCanvas`): DOM/CSS all healthy (canvas `computed: none`, fallback `display: block`, image `complete: true / naturalWidth: 257`, no transforms or clip-paths, `elementFromPoint(center)` returns the IMG with no occluder), but the screenshot capture came up blank. The first canvas-fallback on the same page renders the same SVG file fine, and the SVG file itself is valid (10,051 bytes, viewBox correct). Most likely a Chrome-extension screenshot-capture timing race rather than a real rendering bug — flagged for manual eyeball verification in Ray's actual browser.

**Out-of-scope follow-ups surfaced this chat (NOT part of the Phase 7 fix; flagged in `todo.md` for separate-chat decisions):**

1. **`details.toc-card` floating outline overlays canvas-fallback area on mobile.** Auto-injected per-lesson outline `<details class="card toc-card auto-toc">` with `position: sticky`, top:60, z-index 100, ~229 px tall, default-open. On phones it visually covers the canvas-fallback figure when the user scrolls into the demo section. Pre-existing UX issue (existed before Phase 7 — auto-TOC infrastructure shipped in Phase 5). Each render-check page required JS-toggling `.open = false` to see the canvas area cleanly. Worth a focused chat if mobile UX is in scope; possible fixes range from "default-collapsed on mobile" to "fully hidden below 768 px and rely on the existing breadcrumb + section-anchor links".

2. **Canvas demo JS animation loops keep running on mobile when canvas is hidden.** Visible as e.g. `polish_tweening.html` reporting "FPS: 6, Frame Time: 166.7 ms" in its stats panel with no rendering happening (the JS is updating the stats panel but every `ctx.fillRect` etc. is a no-op against a `display: none` canvas), and `ai_state_machines.html` keeping "ATTACK: 1 | PATROL: 1 | IDLE: 1" live counters running. Wasted CPU on phones with no visible effect. Pre-existing across all 53 canvas demos. Easy fix per-lesson: `if (window.matchMedia('(max-width: 768px)').matches) return;` early-out at the top of each animation loop, OR check `!canvas.offsetParent`. Rolling out to 53 canvases is a script-pass, not a manual edit.

3. **Lazy-loading `loading="lazy"` on canvas-fallback `<img>`** is correct behavior — noted only because it caused diagnostic confusion during the render check. Initial JS reads of `img.naturalWidth` returned `0` because the lazy-loaded image hadn't been pulled in yet at the moment of the JS check; after scroll-into-view, the image loaded and `naturalWidth` was the expected value. Not a bug — but **implication for future render checks: query `naturalWidth` AFTER scrolling the image into viewport, not before.**

**Save-first-not-last discipline added (Ray-driven process change).** Chat 23 surfaced the 4th interrupted-artifact case in 7 chats (rate ~57%). Root cause analysis: doc-saves had been ordered *near* the chat-end interruption window even after chat-19 / 21 / 22 reinforcement. Saves consistently survived disk artifacts (SVG, HTML, catalog) but lost narrative writes to status.md and forward-looking todo.md updates. Reversed the discipline: doc updates now happen at milestone boundaries, not chat end. Stub written at chat start; incremental updates after each milestone (build / insert / catalog flip / render-check / etc.). Render-check still tail-end, but the docs already reflect "build done, check pending" if interrupted there.

**`support/session.md` added (Ray-driven process change).** Single-paragraph canonical resume pointer. First file to read on chat start, before `todo.md`. Overwritten at every milestone — does not accumulate history (that's `status.md`'s job). Schema: Chat / Date / Status / Last completed / Next step / Process changes (optional). Goal: make pre-shipped interrupted-chat artifacts impossible to miss on chat resume; give the picking-up assistant the exact resume point in <300 words.

**Five verification points — all clean:**

1. **`#soundCanvas` computed display.** Inline `style="border: 1px solid #333; display: inline-block;"` (the chat-15 inline-display case the `!important` hardening anticipated). `iwin.getComputedStyle(canvas).display: "none"`. **5th lesson confirming the chat-15 `!important` hardening in the field**, after `polish_screenshake.html` chat 18 (`#shakeCanvas`), `ai_behavior_trees.html` chat 20 (`#behaviorCanvas`), `polish_difficulty.html` chat 22 (`#difficultyCanvas`), and now `polish_sound.html` chat 24 (`#soundCanvas`). The hardening is now field-confirmed across 4 different inline-display lessons spanning all of Phase 7's wired-AND-render-checked work.

4. **Canvas-fallback figure (`figure.canvas-fallback`).** `display: block`; sibling of `#soundCanvas` inside `.canvas-wrapper` (`siblingOfCanvas: true`); img `complete: true`, natural 270×150 → rendered 346×192 (same SVG, same dims as Phase 6 fig); concise 74-char alt: "Four stacked audio tracks: music bed, ambient loop, SFX bursts, UI clicks." — matches "concise fallback alt" convention.

5. **Visual gate** (zoom screenshot of iframe area 0,0→380,820): all 5 rows render cleanly. Music = continuous blue sine bed (no gaps, smooth amplitude); Ambient = purple/violet low-amplitude slow drone; SFX = 3 amber damped-oscillation bursts as designed; UI = 4 teal narrow click-spikes; Master = gray summed envelope with the dashed zero-axis through middle (the 5th row that expanded the original 4-track build_concept). All 5 right-side gain labels intact and readable: `−12 dB` (Music), `−18 dB` (Ambient), `−6 dB` (SFX), `−10 dB` (UI), `Σ` (Master — sigma symbol replacing dB on the master-bus row). Master bus sums all four into the output.". No clipping, no overflow, no layout shift.

The tool returned a 144×84 image showing the **parent page's TOC card** instead of the iframe figure — the tool's reported "region (6,161) to (150,245)" suggested input coords were divided by ~2.46. Iframe was confirmed still at viewport (0,0,381,821) with z-index 99999 and the figure correctly placed inside it; parent scroll was 0; nothing visually obstructing in the regular screenshot. **Workaround used:** mounted the SVG inline at native 720×400 directly in the parent page (`<div id="chat26-visual-host" style="position:fixed;top:20px;left:20px;width:720px;height:400px;...">`), took a regular full-viewport screenshot, inspected. This bypasses the iframe entirely for the visual gate while leaving the structural verification (points 1–4) inside the iframe where it belongs. **Lesson for future render-checks:** if the `zoom` action returns unexpected content, fall back to inline-render-in-parent + regular screenshot; the structural points are independent of the visual gate's host strategy.

Recovery from a mid-pipeline auto-compaction is now demonstrated end-to-end: the chat-23 disciplines (save-first-not-last + `support/session.md` as resume pointer + save-first compounding) made the recovery essentially mechanical — read `session.md`, see "✅ chat-start stub logged", run a single disk-state check that confirms the build artifact, verify the artifact's labels match the lesson's canonical terminology, then resume the pipeline at the next pending step. The build narrative above was reconstructed from the on-disk SVG content and the lesson grep — not from any chat-state captured before the interruption — demonstrating that the SVG file itself + the lesson HTML + the catalog JSON form a self-sufficient recovery substrate. **Lesson:** the chat-23 disciplines pay their largest dividend when the interruption falls *between* a non-doc artifact landing on disk and the doc updates that would have recorded its landing. The disk-state check + canonical-terminology cross-check together replace the missing chat history.

**MCP outage observations.** No outages this chat — single `Claude in Chrome:javascript_tool` call (with a kicked-off-then-poll pattern because the tool doesn't accept top-level `await`) and three `Filesystem:edit_file` calls all completed promptly. Maintains the chat-26 "zero outages" baseline after the chat-25 streak of 3 outages-then-recoveries.

**Conventions added this chat (lever proposal in response to interruption pattern).** After the chat closed clean, Ray asked the meta question: how do we avoid the interruptions that keep happening? Pattern recognition: across chats 14–27, ~5 of 6 fresh-SVG-build chats hit auto-compaction (17/19/21/23/27 yes, 25 no), while 0 of 5 render-check chats did (18/20/22/24/26). Build chats are structurally heavier — the heavy reads (target lesson HTML, precedent lesson HTML, precedent SVG, all full-read) plus the multi-KB chat-close narrative dump both land in build chats. **Four new conventions added in response, all effective chat 28+** (durable bullets in the Conventions section below): (1) default to `head`/`tail`/`view_range` reads; (2) keep `status.md` chat-N section concise (~1.5 KB target, not the 7 KB chat-25/26/27 sections grew to) — disk artifacts are the source of truth, narrative is annotation; (3) intermediate catalog status `built_unwired_chat_N` between SVG-on-disk and wire-complete, so the catalog records the build before the wire/save spike; (4) slim the chat-N+1 kickoff prompt to ~500 bytes (build chats) or modestly longer (render-check chats need explicit visual-gate content lists). Two further levers kept in reserve in case 1–4 don't move the needle: split build/wire across chats N and N+1 (build alone is lightest possible, wire+catalog-finalize moves to N+1); use `bash_tool` on a one-time-copied project for cheap project-wide grep without loading files into context. Catalog schema_notes updated separately to document the new `built_unwired_chat_N` status form.

Chat-28 prompt draft + conventions update both happen after this status.md write.)*

**Milestone 3 — getBBox text-overflow pre-clear (chat-20 mandatory).** Kicked-off-then-poll. **No `requestAnimationFrame` defensive wait** — chat-31 finding settled in chat 32. **First pass walked 58 text/tspan nodes and caught 1 "overflow"** that turned out to be a **false positive**: the em-dash glyph in the empty Accessory slot was inside a `<g transform="translate(530, 358)">` group, so `getBBox()` returned its bbox in the LOCAL (transformed) coordinate space (x=-9.52, y=-13.22, w=19.22, h=23.9 — a glyph centered roughly on local origin), not the SVG-root coordinate space the pre-clear walker compares against viewBox edges. Real rendered position was around (530, 364), well inside the viewBox. **chat-33 finding:** the chat-31/32 pre-clear walker doesn't transform-aware — it works for top-level text but reports false positives for text inside `<g transform="...">`. **Fix: moved the em-dash text out of the transform group** (changed the surrounding `<g>` so the dashed-circle stays inside the transform but the text now uses absolute coords `x="530" y="364"`). Three other transform groups in the SVG (sword glyph, armor chest-plate, gold-counter context) contain only shapes (rect/polygon/path/circle/line), no text — clean. **Re-run on the fixed SVG: 0 overflows, all four tightest margins healthy.** Tightest right 52.02 px ("Stats include equipment bonuses" centered footer caption at y=423), tightest bottom 14.4 px (same caption — sits 14.4 px above the viewBox bottom), tightest left 21.48 px ("ATTRIBUTES" sub-header at x=22, near-edge content as expected), tightest top 12.05 px ("STATS & VITALS" header text at y=24, font-size 11). All four are wider than chat-31's tightest right of 5.11 px and chat-30's tightest top of 9.01 px — no near-edge cases here. **Timing:** elapsed 315.3 ms (first run, 1 overflow detected), 319.1 ms (third run, 0 overflows after fix) — reproducibly ~315 ms across multiple cold-fetch runs on this active foreground tab, matching chat-31's 315.2 ms almost exactly DESPITE the absence of `requestAnimationFrame` defensive waits. **Validate-or-revise on the chat-31 rAF-removal finding:** **partial revision needed.** The chat-32 narrative attributed the 4.6 ms vs 315.2 ms speedup to rAF removal, but chat 33 with no rAF, an active foreground tab (no rAF stall to dodge), and a fresh-but-dev-served SVG still measures ~315 ms. The most likely explanation: Live Server emits `Cache-Control: no-store` so every `fetch('/images/components/...svg')` is a cold disk hit, and chat 32's 4.6 ms must have come from a hot-cache state or a different timing baseline (perhaps measuring just the parse+walk, not the fetch). **Restated finding:** rAF removal is still the right convention (rAF DOES stall on backgrounded tabs and getBBox triggers layout itself, no defensive wait needed) — but the dramatic 68× speedup chat 32 reported is not the rAF-removal-alone steady-state; cache state matters too. Steady-state cold-fetch pre-clear timing is in the 100–300 ms range and is dominated by fetch + parse, not the bbox walk itself. Documenting both findings (transform-text false positive + cold-fetch timing) in the chat-close validate-or-revise.

**Milestone 1 — `sprite_loading_images.html`.** Region-scoped read of the lesson body (`head 130` for Photo Album Analogy / image-format cutout-sticker framing / pixel-grid SVG / mermaid concept tree / Basic Image Loading code; `tail 120` already in context from the M0 batched read covering Common Image Problems / Practice Exercises Try-These-Challenges / Key Takeaways / chat-39 TBD section / What's Next / lesson-nav). Lesson topics richly support a 'cache the spin, skip the tax' framing because the most pedagogically high-value Common Image Problems entries (Black Boxes from forgetting `convert_alpha()` on transparent PNGs / Slow Performance from transforming every frame / Memory Issues from re-loading the same file) ALL fold into one ~30-line demo. **Picked exercise + 3 quiz topics from the lesson's actual content** (not invented): exercise = 'Spinning Sprite — Pre-Rotate Once, Blit Forever' — load `star.png` ONCE with `.convert_alpha()`, pre-compute 36 rotated copies via `[pygame.transform.rotate(original, a) for a in range(0, 360, 10)]` at startup, then in the game loop pick the cached frame by `index = (pygame.time.get_ticks() // 50) % 36` and blit it centred on the screen using `frame.get_rect(center=(400, 300))`, with a live FPS readout in the corner via `clock.get_fps()` to prove the cache keeps the loop pinned at 60 FPS. Q1 = `convert_alpha()` vs `.convert()` distinction on PNGs with transparency (Black Boxes pitfall: plain `.convert()` drops the alpha channel and renders transparent pixels as solid black; `.convert_alpha()` preserves per-pixel alpha AND re-formats for display speed). Q2 = Cache transformations: pre-rotate to a list of N angle copies ONCE rather than calling `pygame.transform.rotate` every frame (Slow Performance pitfall + Performance Tips 'Cache Transformations: Don't rotate/scale every frame' + Key Takeaway 'Cache transformed images instead of recreating' — rotate is per-pixel CPU work, full re-raster every call). Q3 = Preload pattern for many instances of the same sprite (Memory Issues pitfall: loading `enemy.png` inside `Enemy.__init__` for 50 enemies costs 50× the disk I/O + decode AND allocates 50 identical Surfaces; load once at module/class level, share the Surface across instances since blit doesn't mutate). Single `Filesystem:edit_file` call swapped the entire chat-39 TBD `<section class="lesson-section">…</section>` block for the real content, preserving the outer wrapper and full-stem h2 id `practice-exercise-build-sprite-loading-images` per Finding 9. h2 text content extended from the bare TBD `Practice Exercise` to descriptive `Practice Exercise: Cache the Spin, Skip the Tax` (matching the chat-40 cohort-1 pattern of giving each exercise a memorable title — cohort-1 used 'Draw a Simple Scene' / 'Two Input Styles in One Program' / 'AABB Collision in 30 Lines' / 'SFX, Music, and Volume Together'). **Milestone 2 — `sprite_animation.html`.** Region-scoped read of the lesson body already in M0 batched-read context (full lesson body retrieved including Flipbook Analogy / sprite-sheet SVG / mermaid concept tree / Interactive Animation Demo canvas+JS / Basic Frame Animation `AnimatedSprite` class / `TimedAnimation` class / `AnimationStateMachine` class with `add_animation` + `change_state` + `update` / Advanced Animation Techniques / Performance Tips / Common Animation Principles / chat-39 TBD section). Lesson has unusually rich pedagogy because it sets up an explicit hierarchy: basic frame-counter pattern (frame-rate-tied) → time-based pattern with `dt` and `frame_duration` in ms (frame-rate-independent) → state-machine pattern with multiple animations and `change_state` reset semantics. **Picked exercise + 3 quiz topics from the lesson's actual content** (not invented): exercise = 'Idle ↔ Walk — A Frame-Rate-Independent Cycle' — two animation states (Idle: 4 frames @ 200 ms; Walk: 6 frames @ 100 ms) driven by held LEFT/RIGHT arrow keys, with `dt = clock.tick(60)` as the wall-clock time source and `a["t"] += dt` against `a["ms_per_frame"]` for frame advance; on state change, reset the NEW state's `i` and `t` both to 0 (the lesson's `AnimationStateMachine.change_state()` reset pattern); on frame-index overflow, wrap to 0 (loop=True) or clamp to len-1 (loop=False) per the `update()` end-of-animation branch. Frames programmatically generated via a `frames(n, color)` helper using sin-bob displacement so no external image assets are required. Q1 = frame-rate-independent timing using `dt` accumulation against ms `frame_duration` vs the broken counter-increment pattern (Performance Tips 'Frame Rate Independence: Use delta time for timing'; the lesson contrasts basic `AnimatedSprite`'s `animation_counter += animation_speed` against `TimedAnimation`'s `time_since_last_frame += dt`). Q2 = state-change reset semantics inside `change_state()` (must set both `current_frame = 0` and `timer = 0` on the new state, otherwise it starts mid-cycle wherever it was last left — the explicit reset is in the lesson's class definition with a `# Reset new animation` comment). Q3 = end-of-animation branch in `update()`: `loop=True` wraps `current_frame` back to 0 (continuous cycles like walk/idle); `loop=False` clamps at `len(frames) - 1` (one-shot animations like attack/jump-land hold their last frame and signal completion — the 'Could trigger animation complete event here' comment in the lesson code marks the back-to-idle hook). Single `Filesystem:edit_file` call swapped the entire chat-39 TBD `<section>` block for the real content, preserving the outer wrapper and full-stem h2 id `practice-exercise-build-sprite-animation` per Finding 9; h2 text content extended from `Practice Exercise` to descriptive `Practice Exercise: Two States, One dt`. **Milestone 1 — `pygame_basics_drawing.html`.** Region-scoped read of the lesson body (`head 90` for coords intro + mermaid; `tail 110` covered the Practice Exercises Try-These-Challenges block + Common Mistakes + Key Takeaways + the chat-39-injected TBD section + What's Next + lesson-nav). Lesson topics rich and well-scoped: top-left-origin coordinate system (mermaid diagram + 'Y might feel backwards!' callout); 6 drawing primitives (rect / circle / polygon / line / ellipse / arc) already visualised by the chat-20 `pygame-primitives.svg`; sprites + sprite groups for managing many sprites; 5 Common Mistakes (forgetting flip / wrong coords / not clearing screen / loading in loop / forgetting convert). **Picked exercise + 3 quiz topics from the lesson's actual content** (not invented):

- **Exercise: 'A Sun, a Hill, and a House'** — still scene combining filled `pygame.draw.rect` (ground + house body) + filled `pygame.draw.circle` (sun) + non-zero `width` `pygame.draw.rect` re-draw (house outline) + `pygame.draw.polygon` (triangular roof). 8-step instructions, hint that walks through Y-down placement and the polygon-vertex convention, full ~35-line example solution with named colour tuples and inline phase comments mirroring the chat-38 pilot's solution structure.
- **Q1: Coordinate system** — `(0, 0)` at top-left, Y grows down. Maps directly to Common Mistakes #2 (\"Wrong coordinate system: Remember Y increases downward!\").
- **Q2: Optional integer `width`** — omitted or 0 = filled, >= 1 = outline at that line thickness; same convention across rect / circle / polygon / ellipse / arc. Reinforced by the existing `pygame-primitives.svg` bottom strip (\"An optional integer width as the last argument draws an outline instead of filling the shape\").
- **Q3: `Surface.convert()` / `convert_alpha()` performance** — re-stores surface in display's native pixel format so blits become a fast memory copy. Maps directly to Common Mistakes #5 (\"Forgetting convert(): Huge performance impact\").

**Single `Filesystem:edit_file` call** swapped the entire chat-39-injected `<section class="lesson-section">…</section>` TBD block (uniquely identified by h2 id `practice-exercise-build-pygame-basics-drawing`) for the real Exercise + 3-question Quiz section; outer wrapper + h2 id preserved exactly.
