**Milestone 2 — `pygame_basics_input.html`.** Region-scoped read of the lesson body (`head 90` for opening + Restaurant Analogy + the canonical event-vs-state mermaid; `tail 120` covered the gamepad/joystick code + Key Takeaways + the chat-39-injected TBD section + What's Next + lesson-nav). Lesson maps cleanly to the canonical pygame teaching pattern for input — the Restaurant Analogy frames events as 'a waiter taking individual orders' (discrete) vs state-based as 'a buffet where you continuously check what's available' (continuous), and the Key Takeaways enumerates both styles explicitly with their canonical use cases (events: jump / shoot / menu; state polling: movement / aiming). **Picked exercise + 3 quiz topics from the lesson's actual content:**

- **Exercise: 'Move and Jump' — Two Input Styles in One Program** — player square moves continuously via `pygame.key.get_pressed()` for K_LEFT/K_RIGHT (state-based) AND jumps once per spacebar tap via `KEYDOWN` event for K_SPACE (event-based), with simple gravity and a ground clamp so the asymmetry between the two styles becomes physically visible (jump impulse fires once per intentional press, not 60 times per second while spacebar is held). Six-step instructions, hint that explicitly walks through the 'try moving the jump into get_pressed()' anti-pattern to make the difference concrete, full ~40-line example solution with both input branches inline-commented as DISCRETE and CONTINUOUS.
- **Q1: Event-based use case (canonical)** — jump/shoot/menu = events; movement/cursor-following = state polling. Maps to Key Takeaways #1+#2 and Restaurant Analogy directly.
- **Q2: `pygame.key.get_pressed()` return shape** — sequence-like object indexed by keycode constants (`keys[pygame.K_LEFT]`), True while held, read once per frame. Distractors test the common confusions with `event.get()` (events not states) and `event.key` (single keycode comparison).
- **Q3: KEYDOWN-fires-once vs get_pressed()-fires-every-frame asymmetry** — why a jump impulse belongs in the KEYDOWN branch. The explanation makes the foot-gun physical: re-applying `vy = JUMP_VELOCITY` 60×/sec while the spacebar is held launches the player off-screen. Distractors test the wrong intuitions (performance, get_pressed missing keys) so the correct answer must engage with the timing semantics.

**Note on the example solution's `>` character:** the example uses Python's `if y > GROUND_Y:` clamp; encoded in the HTML as `&gt;` per HTML escaping rules to render correctly inside `<pre><code>`. Same encoding pattern used by the chat-38 pilot for its `<`-flavored Python (none in pilot, but consistent if/when needed). **Single `Filesystem:edit_file` call** swapped the chat-39-injected `<section class="lesson-section">…</section>` TBD block (h2 id `practice-exercise-build-pygame-basics-input`) for real content; outer wrapper + h2 id preserved exactly. **Catalog flip** via single `Filesystem:edit_file` call: `pygame_basics_input.html` `quiz_drafted` → `done` with `completed_chat: 40` + filled `exercise_card_objective` (one-sentence framing tying the asymmetry to the demo's physical visibility) + 3-element `quiz_topics` list with parenthetical lesson-anchor references. **Phase 8 status delta:** 2/64 done + 62/64 quiz_drafted → **3/64 done** + 61/64 quiz_drafted; pygame_basics module now 3/5 done (game_loop chat 38 + drawing chat 40 + input chat 40), 2 remaining (collision + sound). **35th consecutive save-first-compounding step** (lesson HTML edit + catalog flip + this M2 narrative all landed in M2). Pacing observation: chat-40 M0+M1+M2 ran cleanly with the brief's per-lesson workflow holding precisely — region-scoped read → pick exercise+topics → single-call lesson edit → single-call catalog flip → narrative; no surprises so far, no carry-forward findings beyond chat-40 Finding 9 (cosmetic h2 id stem divergence) logged at M0.

**Milestone 3 — `pygame_basics_collision.html`.** Region-scoped read of the lesson body (`head 100` for opening + Security Check Analogy + collision-types mermaid + AABB intro; `tail 110` covered the Practice Exercises Challenge-Yourself block + Pro Tips + Key Takeaways + the chat-39-injected TBD section + What's Next + lesson-nav). Lesson centres on the AABB-first principle — the Security Check Analogy frames bounding-box rectangles as the 'metal detector gate' (quick but not precise) vs pixel-perfect as the 'full body scan' (precise but slow), the mermaid taxonomy lists Rectangle/Circle/Pixel-Perfect/Polygon, the AABB section opens the lesson body proper, and the Pro Tips list explicitly leads with 'Start Simple: Use rectangles first, optimize later if needed.' **Picked exercise + 3 quiz topics from the lesson's actual content:**

- **Exercise: 'Coin Collector' — AABB Collision in 30 Lines** — top-down player Rect moves with arrow keys (state-polling recap from the chat-40 M2 input lesson) and collects 5 scattered coin Rects via a single list-comprehension `coins = [c for c in coins if not player.colliderect(c)]`. Uses `pygame.Rect` objects for both player and coins (so `colliderect` and `clamp_ip` come for free), `player.clamp_ip(screen.get_rect())` to keep the player on-screen, and 7-step instructions that walk through the Rect-object choice + the colliderect filter pattern + the smaller-hitbox tip in the Hint via `rect.inflate(-8, -8)`. ~35-line example solution that explicitly recaps the input lesson's get_pressed() arrow-key movement.
- **Q1: Why AABB rectangles first** — lesson's Pro Tip #1 'Start Simple' + Security Check Analogy. Distractors test the wrong reasons (GPU rendering speed, rotation handling) so the correct answer must engage with the cost asymmetry ('cheap enough to run on every pair every frame, most 2D games never feel the lack of precision').
- **Q2: `a.colliderect(b)` return shape** — returns a bool, not a Rect (that's `a.clip(b)`) and not a point-test (that's `rect.collidepoint((x,y))`). The explanation calls out both adjacent APIs explicitly so the test isn't just rote.
- **Q3: Smaller-hitbox-than-sprite rule** — Pro Tip #3 ('better game feel'). Distractors test the wrong intuitions (performance gain, rendering tearing) so the correct answer must engage with the perceptual asymmetry between 'a hit looks like a hit' and 'colliderect returned True'. Explanation gives the canonical implementation hint (`rect.inflate(-N, -N)`).

**Single `Filesystem:edit_file` call** swapped the chat-39-injected `<section class="lesson-section">…</section>` TBD block (h2 id `practice-exercise-build-pygame-basics-collision`) for real content; outer wrapper + h2 id preserved exactly. **Catalog flip** via single `Filesystem:edit_file` call: `pygame_basics_collision.html` `quiz_drafted` → `done` with `completed_chat: 40` + filled `exercise_card_objective` (one-sentence framing tying the demo to the AABB-in-30-lines goal and the get_pressed recap) + 3-element `quiz_topics` list with parenthetical lesson-anchor references including the Security Check Analogy callout. **Phase 8 status delta:** 3/64 done + 61/64 quiz_drafted → **4/64 done** + 60/64 quiz_drafted; pygame_basics module now 4/5 done (game_loop + drawing + input + collision), 1 remaining (sound). **36th consecutive save-first-compounding step** (lesson HTML edit + catalog flip + this M3 narrative all landed in M3).

**Milestone 4 — `pygame_basics_sound.html`.** Region-scoped read of the lesson body (`head 130` for opening + Movie Theater Analogy + audio-system mermaid + mixer setup snippet + Sound API intro; `tail 120` covered Pro Tips + Common Pitfalls + Practice Exercises + Key Takeaways + the chat-39-injected TBD section + What's Next + lesson-nav). Lesson is denser than the previous three — it teaches both halves of `pygame.mixer` (Sound objects for short multi-instance SFX, `pygame.mixer.music` module for streamed background tracks) plus the explicit `set_num_channels(8)` setup pattern, plus a Pro-Tips list with concrete audio-design rules ('music quieter than SFX', 'every action gets audio feedback', 'preload to avoid stuttering'), plus a Common Pitfalls list anchored on lag/crackling/silent-failure. **Picked exercise + 3 quiz topics from the lesson's actual content:**

- **Exercise: 'Sound Board' — SFX, Music, and Volume Together** — single-window demo where K_1/K_2/K_3 play three preloaded `pygame.mixer.Sound` objects and K_M toggles a looping `pygame.mixer.music` background track via `pause()`/`unpause()`, with per-source `set_volume()` calls demonstrating the 'music quieter than SFX' pyramid. ~45-line example solution explicitly comments the four numbered phases (mixer init + channels / preload Sound objects / load + play music / event-driven trigger). 6-step instructions guide the user through providing their own audio assets (freesound.org / jsfxr.me referenced as the lesson convention since pygame tutorials universally assume user-supplied audio files — mirrors the lesson body's own `jump.wav`/`coin.ogg`/`explosion.mp3` placeholders).
- **Q1: Sound vs music architectural distinction** — Sound loads entire file into memory for multi-instance playback (short SFX); music streams from disk one track at a time (long background music). Maps directly to Key Takeaway #2. Distractors test the wrong intuitions (alias for same API, format-based selection) so the correct answer must engage with the in-memory-vs-streamed split.
- **Q2: Preload Sound objects ONCE before the loop** — constructing a Sound reads + decodes the file each time; per-event construction causes audible lag at exactly the moment of input. Maps to Key Takeaway #4 + Common Pitfall #1 ('Lag/Delay: Increase buffer size or preload sounds'). Distractors test wrong reasons (resource conflict, auto-play behaviour) so the correct answer must engage with the disk-and-decode cost.
- **Q3: `set_num_channels(N)` channel semantics** — N parallel SFX voices on the mixer; when all busy, new `.play()` STEALS the oldest channel rather than failing (audible as cut-off sounds in busy games); independent of `pygame.mixer.music`. The set_num_channels(8) line is right there in the lesson's setup snippet, so this question forces engagement with what that line actually does. Distractors test confusion with stereo channels and with hard-cap-on-Sound-objects misconceptions.

**Single `Filesystem:edit_file` call** swapped the chat-39-injected `<section class="lesson-section">…</section>` TBD block (h2 id `practice-exercise-build-pygame-basics-sound`) for real content; outer wrapper + h2 id preserved exactly. **Catalog flip** via single `Filesystem:edit_file` call: `pygame_basics_sound.html` `quiz_drafted` → `done` with `completed_chat: 40` + filled `exercise_card_objective` (one-sentence framing tying the demo to BOTH halves of `pygame.mixer` + the volume balancing Pro Tip + the channels setup) + 3-element `quiz_topics` list with parenthetical lesson-anchor references including Key Takeaway and Common Pitfall callouts. **Phase 8 status delta:** 4/64 done + 60/64 quiz_drafted → **5/64 done** + 59/64 quiz_drafted; **pygame_basics module is now 5/5 done — first complete module in Phase 8.** **37th consecutive save-first-compounding step** (lesson HTML edit + catalog flip + this M4 narrative all landed in M4). **Milestone 2 — dry-run across 64 lessons (first pass surfaced Finding 7; regex patched; second-pass verification queued for Ray's terminal).** First-pass dry-run reported `would-update: 58 / already-injected: 1 / no-anchor: 5 / anchors used: what-s-next=58, lesson-nav=0`. **Pilot idempotency-skip clean** — `pygame_basics_game_loop.html` shows `already-injected`, smoke-test of M1 logic passes. **All 58 successful matches used the `what-s-next` anchor;** the `lesson-nav` fallback never fired in the first pass. **Five lessons hit `no-anchor`** — `genres_puzzle_python.html`, `genres_strategy_python.html`, `genres_tower_defense_python.html`, `polish_playtesting.html`, `publishing_updates.html`. Tail-reads on two of them (`genres_puzzle_python.html` + `polish_playtesting.html`) confirmed both DO have `<nav class="lesson-nav" aria-label="Lesson navigation">` at the close — they just lack the `<h2 id="what-s-next">` h2 because they're section-end or appendix-style lessons (`polish_playtesting.html` closes the polish section with a Section Summary + "Continue to the next section..." prose; the `_python.html` files are code-dump appendices to their parent lessons). The lesson-nav fallback was supposed to catch exactly these cases. **Phase-8 Finding 7 logged: 5 lessons are section-end / appendix-style and skip the What's Next h2; the lesson-nav fallback path is the only anchor for them.** A second sub-finding emerged from the diagnostic: **the original `LESSON_NAV_RE` regex had a `\b` bug** — `r'<nav\s+class="lesson-nav"\b'` requires a word boundary after the closing `"`, but `"` is non-word and the next char (a space before `aria-label=...`) is also non-word, so no word boundary exists and the regex matched nothing. The bug was silent because the pilot and the 58 successful first-pass matches all used the preferred `what-s-next` anchor; only the 5 lessons that genuinely needed the fallback exposed it. **Patched the regex to `r'<nav\s+class="lesson-nav"'`** — the closing quote inside the literal already enforces exact class match (no risk of false-matching e.g. `lesson-navigation`), and an inline comment documents the bug + the M2 catch-point for downstream readers. Patch landed via `Filesystem:edit_file` against the live `support/inject_pedagogy_scaffold.py`. **29th consecutive save-first-compounding step** (M2 first-pass diagnostic + regex patch + this finding paragraph land = M2's narrative on disk before the second-pass re-run; a re-run regression would be caught against the same M2 narrative slot rather than re-discovered fresh). Second-pass dry-run queued for Ray's terminal: expected counts 58 + 5 = 63 `would-update` + 1 `already-injected` + 0 `no-anchor` + 0 `missing` + anchors used `what-s-next=58, lesson-nav=5`. **Per-lesson h2 ids reviewed for collisions — zero across the 58 first-pass matches** (each id is `practice-exercise-build-<unique-stem>` since stems are derived from unique filenames; the only collision risk would be a pre-existing `practice-exercise-build-<same-stem>` h2 in a lesson body which is impossible since the chat-37 audit confirmed 0/64 lessons have any pre-existing `practice-exercise-build-*` id). **Per-lesson coexistence with pre-existing inline `Practice Exercise / Try It / Challenge` h2 (Finding 3) verified clean** — the pilot demonstrates the pattern (`<h2 id="practice-exercise-modify-the-loop">` mid-lesson coexists with `<h2 id="practice-exercise-build-game-loop">` bottom-of-lesson; distinct ids, both render); the 60/64 lessons with the inline pattern follow the same rule by construction.

**Verification re-run confirmed expected counts byte-for-byte:** `would-update: 63 / already-injected: 1` (no `no-anchor` line in summary at all this pass) / `anchors used: what-s-next=58, lesson-nav=5`. All 58 originally-matching lessons stayed on the `what-s-next` anchor (regex patch surgically widened only the fallback path; preferred-path matching is untouched). The 5 previously-broken lessons all now show `anchor=lesson-nav` with the expected `practice-exercise-build-<stem>` ids: `genres-puzzle-python` / `genres-strategy-python` / `genres-tower-defense-python` / `polish-playtesting` / `publishing-updates`. Pilot stays `already-injected`. M2 closes clean.

The pilot lesson received no `.bak` because the script returned `already-injected` before reaching the backup branch. **Spot-check on two lessons** (one per anchor type) confirms the injected section landed in the right relative position and contains the expected markup. (1) **`sprite_animation.html` (preferred-anchor `what-s-next` case):** new section sits between Key Takeaways `</div>` and `<h2 id="what-s-next">`; h2 id is `practice-exercise-build-sprite-animation`; three TBD quiz-question blocks render identically to the pilot template. (2) **`polish_playtesting.html` (fallback-anchor `lesson-nav` case):** new section sits between the closing `</div>` of the section-end card and `<nav class="lesson-nav">`; h2 id is `practice-exercise-build-polish-playtesting`; three TBD quiz-question blocks identical. **Phase-8 Finding 8 logged: cosmetic insertion artifacts in the injected sections.** Three non-rendering sub-issues visible across both spot-checks: (a) **one extra blank line above the section** — 2 blank lines between previous content and the new `<section>` instead of the pilot's 1, caused by `render_section()`'s leading `\n` combining with the content's existing trailing newline at line_start; (b) **indent mismatch with the host lesson body** — the injected section is hardcoded to 8-space outer indent (matching the pilot), but some lessons like `sprite_animation.html` use 4-space outer indent for their lesson body; HTML doesn't care about whitespace so rendering is unaffected; (c) **orphaned `<!-- Lesson Navigation -->` comment in the 5 lesson-nav fallback cases** — the pre-existing comment that was originally a label for the nav element is now positioned above the new section instead of above the nav, since the section was inserted at the start of the line containing `<nav>` (the comment line precedes that). All three sub-issues are purely source-view cosmetics with zero behavioral or visual rendering impact; logged as Phase 9 lint candidates if Ray ever wants source-tidy passes. Catalog status not changed in M3 (M3 only mutates lesson HTML; catalog batch flip is M4). **30th consecutive save-first-compounding step.** *(Spot-check method note: tail-90 reads on the two spot-check lessons were sufficient to verify both the injection point and the section body without full-file reads, per chat-27 region-scoped-read discipline.)*

Differs from python_intro's at-the-very-end placement, but pygame_gamedev has a forward-link wrap-up that python_intro doesn't — What's Next? should remain the lesson's last word. **Quiz topics chosen** from lesson's actual content (3 of 5 kickoff candidates): Q1 = `pygame.event.get()` event-pump / OS-responsiveness (lesson explicitly mentions “OS will think the game has crashed”), Q2 = `screen.fill()` vs `pygame.display.flip()` back-buffer / double-buffering distinction, Q3 = `clock.tick(60)` semantics (lesson explicitly says “Always use frame rate limiting”). All 9 buttons have `data-correct` true/false; incorrect buttons have `data-hint`; correct buttons have `data-explanation`. Markup verbatim follows chat-37 M1 python_intro template: outer `<section class="lesson-section">`, exercise card `<div class="card card-info">` with h3+Objective+Instructions+Hint details+Solution details, quiz card `<div class="card quiz-container"><h3>🎯 Quick Quiz</h3>` with 3 `<div class="quiz-question">` blocks. **22nd consecutive save-first-compounding step.** Lesson HTML edit landed in one `Filesystem:edit_file` call, ~5.6 KB net addition (lesson grew 21,608 → ~27 KB).

The `create_file` tool's success message is misleading on UNC paths — it returns `File created successfully: <UNC path>` even though nothing landed at that path. Fix codified in chat-39 next-chat-prompt + session.md + todo.md carry-forward disciplines for downstream chats. **25th consecutive save-first-compounding step** (M4 land = 5 file ops, all on the WSL filesystem, post-recovery; counted as one milestone per chat-37/38 M4 convention).

### Original Phase 7 sketch (kept for reference)

`<canvas>` elements are hidden on mobile via `enhanced.css` rule
`canvas { display: none !important; }` (the `!important` was added chat 15 — see
*Phase 7 progress (chat 15)* above for the specificity bug it solves). The
existing `.mobile-diagram-note` is a generic apology, not a substitute.

**Scope (post-Phase-6 audit numbers):**
- **53 canvas demos across 64 lessons** (84% of lessons have at least one canvas).
- **15 canvas-heavy lessons (>400k px²)** — priority bucket where the mobile loss is largest.
- **16 lessons already have a Phase 6 SVG** that may double as a partial fallback for an adjacent canvas.
- **48 lessons have no static visuals** (mermaid only).

**Approach (sketch — now realized via chat 12 catalog + script):**
- Script wraps every `<canvas>` in a `<div class="canvas-with-fallback">` containing canvas + a static SVG (from Phase 6 library) + descriptive caption.
- CSS swaps which is visible based on viewport width.
- Per-lesson mapping in `phase7-canvas-fallback-catalog.json`.

## Phase 8 — Pedagogy upgrade (per-lesson, hand work)

Add formal "Practice Exercise" + 3-question quiz section to each lesson, mirroring
python_intro's pattern.

**Quiz markup (from python_intro):**
```html
<div class="card quiz-container">
    <h3>🎯 Quick Quiz</h3>
    <div class="quiz-question">
        <p><strong>Question 1:</strong> ...</p>
        <div class="quiz-options">
            <button class="quiz-option" data-correct="false" data-hint="...">A) ...</button>
            <button class="quiz-option" data-correct="true" data-explanation="...">B) ...</button>
            <button class="quiz-option" data-correct="false" data-hint="...">C) ...</button>
        </div>
        <div class="quiz-feedback"></div>
    </div>
</div>
```

The quiz JS is already in `js/course-enhancements.js` for python_intro but **NOT
in python_gamedev's `course-enhancements.js`** (which is mostly Prism). Will
need to either port the quiz init code or add it to nav-enhancements.js.

**Process:** could scaffold with a script that injects empty quiz/exercise
templates into each lesson, then humans fill in actual questions. Or do it
purely by hand a few lessons at a time.

---

## Phase 9 — Code quality pass

Lint script flags inconsistent style across lessons:
- Mixed dataclass usage (some lessons use `@dataclass`, some don't)
- Inconsistent type hints
- Drifting class naming conventions
- Long monolithic class examples vs. focused snippets

Hand rewrites of worst offenders. Could use `pylint` or `ruff` programmatically
but the variance is more about pedagogical consistency than code correctness.

## Smaller items mentioned but not scoped yet

- **Standardize breadcrumb format** — each lesson hand-codes its own crumb
  ("Section 4: Game Physics - Lesson 5", "Advanced Module - Section 1: Advanced
  Graphics - Lesson 2"). Script could rewrite using a JSON catalog of
  module/section/lesson structure.
- **"Lesson X of N in <Module>" indicator** — same JSON catalog drives this.
- **Index.html theme polish** — index has its own purple/teal hero in inline
  `<style>`. Currently doesn't flip on theme toggle. Either add `--include-index`
  to the next inject script run, or hand-edit index's inline styles to use
  CSS variables.
- **Path style inconsistency** — some lessons use absolute `/styles/main.css`,
  others relative `styles/main.css`. `inject_main_nav.py` handled this per-file
  for new script tags, but the existing CSS/icon links remain mixed. Script
  could normalize to all-relative for portability.
- **Decide fate of `_python.html` companion files** — standalone lessons or
  appendix code? If appendix, should they be linked from their parent lesson
  rather than appearing in the navigation as siblings?
- **(Surfaced chat 15) `details.toc-card` mobile overlay.** The auto-TOC
  `<details class="card toc-card auto-toc">` (from Phase 5 nav-enhancements.js)
  is sticky at top:60, z-index 100, ~229 px tall, default-open, and visually
  covers the canvas-fallback area on mobile. Pre-existing UX issue. Possible
  fixes: default-collapsed below 768 px, fully hidden below 768 px, or shrink
  the sticky height.
- **(Surfaced chat 15) Canvas demo JS animation loops on mobile.** All 53
  canvas demos keep their animation loops running even when the canvas is
  `display: none`. Wasted CPU on phones. Easy per-lesson fix
  (`if (matchMedia('(max-width: 768px)').matches) return;` early-out) but
  rolling out to 53 canvases is a script-pass.

---

## Conventions / things to remember

- **Filesystem tool > computer use tool** for all WSL file ops in this project
- **Prefer `edit_file` over `write_file`** for existing files (less rewrite risk; `session.md` is the explicit exception — it gets fully overwritten every milestone)
- **Default to region-scoped reads (chat 27 added; effective chat 28+).** For lesson HTML, precedent lesson HTML, and precedent SVG, use `head` / `tail` / `view_range` to read only the relevant region — not the full file. Build chats were consuming 30–50% more input tokens than necessary by full-reading files when only ~50 lines were relevant. Triggers: target lesson → grep for `svg-wrapper` and the canvas-wrapper anchor first, then `view_range` read of the mermaid-and-canvas-wrapper region only; precedent lesson → same; precedent SVG → header comment (the build narrative) + `tail 5` to confirm closing `</svg>`, body skipped unless visual-language reuse is genuinely needed. Full-file reads should be a deliberate escalation, not the default.
- **Keep `status.md` chat-N sections concise (chat 27 added; effective chat 28+).** Aim for ~1.5 KB per chat-N section, not the 7 KB chat-25/26/27 sections grew to. The walkthrough doesn't need to be exhaustive — it needs to be enough that an interrupted chat's recovery can pick up state. The artifacts on disk (SVG, lesson HTML, catalog JSON, this `status.md` itself once trimmed) ARE the source of truth; the narrative is annotation, not duplication. Trim ruthlessly: SVG build details that are visible by reading the SVG header comment don't need to be repeated; getBBox numbers tighter than ~20 px right margin are interesting and should be recorded, anything healthier is just "clean." Save-at-milestones (chat-23 discipline) becomes more powerful when each milestone save is small.
- **Intermediate catalog status `built_unwired_chat_N` (chat 27 added; effective chat 29+ — the next build chat).** Between SVG file landing on disk and wire+catalog finalize, flip the lesson's catalog entry to `built_unwired_chat_N` immediately after the SVG file is written. If compaction hits between SVG and wire — the dominant failure mode (5/5 interrupted-artifact cases hit exactly this window) — the catalog records the build automatically and recovery is even cheaper than chat 27. Wire completion then flips to `built chat N` as today. New status flow: `needs_new_svg` → `built_unwired_chat_N` → `built chat N`. Schema note added to `support/phase7-canvas-fallback-catalog.json`.
- **Slim chat-N+1 kickoff prompt (chat 27 added; effective chat 28+).** Target ~500 bytes for build-chat kickoffs; modestly longer for render-check kickoffs (the 5 verification points and visual-gate content list need explicit listing). The current 3 KB kickoffs duplicate `session.md` + `todo.md` content; the working files carry the convention details. Kickoff prompt structure: project root + UNC-path reminder; one sentence pointing to `session.md` as resume pointer; one sentence describing the chat-N task; that's it. Everything else lives in `session.md` / `todo.md` / `next-chat-prompt.md`.
- **Stream `status.md` narrative incrementally per milestone (chat 30 added; effective chat 30+).** Don't bunch the chat-N `status.md` narrative as one block at chat close — that's the dominant interruption-loss surface (5 of 6 interrupted chats lost the narrative dump while preserving every other on-disk artifact, including chat 29). Instead, append short prose paragraphs to the chat-N `status.md` section *after each pipeline milestone*: lesson read / `build_concept` refinement / SVG file write / wire / catalog flip / getBBox pre-clear / render-check / etc. Each individual `Filesystem:edit_file` call to `status.md` is small (~150–300 bytes) and ordered *away* from the chat-end interruption window. Per-milestone writes ride alongside the artifact saves they describe and use the same chat-23 save-first principle, but at finer granularity than `session.md` (which still gets a single milestone overwrite per save). The chat-close `status.md` write is then just a short wrap-up paragraph. **Chat-N section structure under this convention:**
  ```
  ### Phase 7 progress (date chat N — task)

  **IN PROGRESS / CLOSED CLEAN.** [one-line headline summary, written at chat start]

  **Milestone 1 — name.** [paragraph appended after milestone 1 completes]

  **Milestone 2 — name.** [paragraph appended after milestone 2 completes]

  …

  **Chat close.** [short wrap-up appended at chat close]
  ```
  Trade-off: more `Filesystem:edit_file` calls per chat, but each call is small and the per-call cost is dramatically lower than the chat-end-blowup cost. Effective chat 30+ — chat 30 (render-check) is the first test bed; chat 31+ build chats are where the bigger interruption-rate dividend is expected. Discipline applies uniformly to build AND render-check chats so it's automatic per chat type, not something each chat has to switch on. **The chat-N section is built as you go, not at the end.**
- **`audit_lessons.py`'s `svg` column counts inline `<svg>` only.** Phase 6 SVGs (delivered as standalone files in `/images/components/` via `<img>`) show up in the `img` column, not `svg`. To count Phase 6 deployments, sum `img` across lessons that received them.
- **Before writing a new SVG, `grep -l 'svg-wrapper'` the target lesson(s).** Pre-staged `<figure class="svg-wrapper">` markup may already dictate filename, layout, or labels. Existing alt text = spec.
- **`canvas { display: none !important; }` is the established mobile-fallback hide rule.** Inline `display:` styles on `<canvas>` tags would otherwise win on specificity (chat 15 finding — 3 of 6 canvases on the chat 13/14 wrapped lessons had inline `display: inline-block`). The `!important` neutralizes any inline override, so when wrapping new canvases for Phase 7 you do NOT need to audit each canvas tag for inline display styles before wrapping. **However, source-level "did the rule exist?" reviews are insufficient — render-check at phone width is mandatory before declaring a Phase 7 wrap done.**
- **Warn when conversation is getting long** rather than letting auto-compaction hit
- **Save-first-not-last (chat 23 added).** Doc updates happen at milestone boundaries, not chat end. Stub `todo.md` + `status.md` writes at chat start; incremental updates after each milestone (build / insert / catalog flip / render-check). Reverses the chat-19/21/22 failure pattern (saves were ordered *near* the interruption window).
- **`support/session.md` is the canonical resume pointer (chat 23 added).** First file to read on every chat start, before `todo.md`. Overwritten at every milestone — single-paragraph snapshot, not accumulating history. Schema: Chat / Date / Status / Last completed / Next step / Process changes (optional). Keep under ~350 words.
- **Don't add content not present in existing lessons** unless explicitly requested
- **Don't add PetalFawnStudio branding** unless explicitly requested
- **Path: `\\wsl$\Ubuntu\…`** not `\\wsl.localhost\Ubuntu\…`
- All injection scripts in this project follow the same shape: idempotent,
  `--dry-run`, `--no-backup`, `.bak` sibling files, color terminal output, summary
  block at end.

---

## Sister projects (for cross-reference)

- **python_intro** — completed, 10 lessons. FAB-collapse TOC done. Hand-coded
  per-lesson TOC. Source of truth for the design system patterns.
- **python_intermediate** — completed, 12 lessons. FAB-collapse TOC done via
  `migrate_toc_summary.py`.
- **python_gamedev** — in progress (this project). Different shape: 64 topic-named
  lessons rather than sequential `lesson_NN.html`, much heavier reliance on
  `<canvas>` interactive demos.
